Bioinformatics 25, 2078–2079 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2777">52</a></sup> to filter out low-quality (mapping quality &lt;30) alignments and the Genome Analysis Toolkit (GATK)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="McKenna, A. et al. The Genome Analysis Toolkit: a MapReduce framework for analyzing next-generation DNA sequencing data. Genome Res. 20, 1297–1303 (2010)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2781">53</a></sup> (<a href="http://www.broadinstitue.org/gatk/">http://www.broadinstitue.org/gatk/</a>) UnifiedGenotypers to call SNPs. The SNPs were filtered using the GATK VariantFiltration program with the following criteria: clusterWindowSize:10, MQ0&gt;=4&amp; ((MQ0/ (1.0* DP)) &gt;0.1), QUAL&lt;50.0, DP&lt; 5. A total of 4,523,444 homozygous SNPs were identified between the parents on 1,386 contigs and used to filter out unmatched SNPs or extremely unevenly distributed SNPs in the RIL population. A total of 4,198,995 filtered SNPs and 2,300 bin markers were obtained on 1,381 contigs for the linkage map construction. Published markers<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Koren, S., Walenz, B. P., Berlin, K., Miller, J. R. &amp; Phillippy, A. M. Canu: scalable and accurate long-read assembly via adaptive k-mer weighting and repeat separation. Genome Res. 27, 722–736 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2793">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Marten, B. &amp; Walter, P. SSPACE-LongRead: scaffolding bacterial draft genomes using long read sequence information. BMC Bioinformatics 15, 211 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2796">20</a></sup> were used to validate the linkage map (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#MOESM1">5</a> and Supplementary Data Set <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#MOESM3">1</a>). Fifty SNP sliding windows were used to create SNP bins to find recombination sites. JoinMap4.1 (<a href="https://www.kyazma.nl/index.php/JoinMap/">https://www.kyazma.nl/index.php/JoinMap/</a>) ML methods were used to cluster the bins into LGs, and then the MstMap<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Wu, Y., Bhat, P. R., Close, T. J. &amp; Lonardi, S. Efficient and accurate construction of genetic linkage maps from the minimum spanning tree of a graph. PLoS Genet. 4, e1000212 (2008)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2813">54</a></sup> (<a href="http://www.mstmap.org/download.html">http://www.mstmap.org/download.html</a>) Kosambi model was used to compute the order of the bins. The final map anchored 1,280 contigs to eight linkage groups.</p><p>To evaluate the assembled genome quality, first we mapped the illumina NGS data to the genome using BWA-mem<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Li, H. Aligning sequence reads, clone sequences and assembly contigs with BWA-MEM. Preprint at arXiv: &#xA;                    https://arxiv.org/abs/1303.3997&#xA;                    &#xA;                   (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2828">51</a></sup> (<a href="http://bio-bwa.sourceforge.net/">http://bio-bwa.sourceforge.net/</a>). Then we aligned the EST sequence download from NCBI (<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nucest/?term=EST%20Antirrhinum">http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nucest/?term=EST%20Antirrhinum</a>) using BLAT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Altschul, S. F. &amp; Gish, W. Local alignment statistics. Methods Enzymo. 266, 460–480 (1996)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2846">55</a></sup>. Finally, we used BUSCO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Simão, F. A. et al. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 3210–3212 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2850">23</a></sup> (<a href="http://busco.ezlab.org">http://busco.ezlab.org, v3</a>) to examine the gene content with Embryophyta odb9 database and parameters. We also used BWA-mem<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Li, H. Aligning sequence reads, clone sequences and assembly contigs with BWA-MEM. Preprint at arXiv: &#xA;                    https://arxiv.org/abs/1303.3997&#xA;                    &#xA;                   (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2862">51</a></sup> with default settings to align three BAC sequences to the assembled genome. GenBank numbers of the three BACs are AY935269.1, FJ404769.1 and FJ404770.1 with lengths of 85, 51 and 111.3 kb, separately.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Gene structure annotation and functional annotation</h3><p>The gene annotation in the <i>A. majus</i> genome was performed by a combination of ab initio and evidence-based methods<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Stanke, M. et al. AUGUSTUS: ab initio prediction of alternative transcripts. Nucleic Acids Res. 34, W435–W439 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2877">24</a></sup>. The protein sequences from three sequenced plants, namely, <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>C. papaya</i> and <i>S. tuberosum</i>, were aligned to the genome using TBLASTN<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Altschul, S. F. &amp; Gish, W. Local alignment statistics. Methods Enzymo. 266, 460–480 (1996)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2891">55</a></sup> with an <i>E</i> value cut-off of 1 × 10<sup>–5</sup>. The homologous genomic sequences were aligned against the matching proteins using GeneWise (<a href="https://www.ebi.ac.uk/Tools/psa/genewise/">https://www.ebi.ac.uk/Tools/psa/genewise/</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Birney, E., Clamp, M. &amp; Durbin, R. GeneWise and Genomewise. Genome Res. 14, 988–995 (2004)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2907">56</a></sup> for accurate spliced alignments. For ab initio prediction, Augustus (<a href="http://augustus.gobics.de">http://augustus.gobics.de</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Stanke, M. et al. AUGUSTUS: ab initio prediction of alternative transcripts. Nucleic Acids Res. 34, W435–W439 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2919">24</a></sup> and GlimmerHMM<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Majoros, W. H., Pertea, M. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics 20, 2878–2879 (2004)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2923">57</a></sup> were run on the repeat masked genome with parameters trained from the closely related species and partial or small genes that had less than 150 bp coding length were discarded. EST was aligned to the genome using BLAT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Kent, W. J. BLAT‐‐the BLAST‐like alignment tool. Genome Res. 12, 656–664 (2002)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2927">58</a></sup> to generate spliced alignments, which were linked according to the overlap using PASA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Campbell, M. A., Haas, B. J., Hamilton, J. P., Mount, S. M. &amp; Buell, C. R. Comprehensive analysis of alternative splicing in rice and comparative analyses with Arabidopsis. BMC Genomics 7, 327 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2931">59</a></sup>. Finally, we aligned all the RNA reads to the reference genome by TopHat<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Trapnell, C., Pachter, L. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. TopHat: discovering splice junctions with RNA-Seq. Bioinformatics 25, 1105–1111 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2935">60</a></sup> (<a href="https://ccb.jhu.edu/software/tophat/index.shtml">https://ccb.jhu.edu/software/tophat/index.shtml</a>), assembled the transcripts using Cufflinks<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Trapnell, C. et al. Transcript assembly and quantification by RNA-Seq reveals unannotated transcripts and isoform switching during cell differentiation. Nat. Biotechnol. 28, 511–515 (2010)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2947">61</a></sup> under default parameters and predicted the open reading frames to get reliable transcripts with HMM-based training parameters. To finalize the gene set, all the predictions were combined using GLEAN<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Christine, G. E. et al. Creating a honey bee consensus gene set. Genome. Biol. 8, R13 (2007)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2951">62</a></sup> to produce the consensus gene sets. On the other hand, another gene annotation in the snapdragon genome was performed using the Gramene pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Liang, C., Mao, L., Ware, D. &amp; Stein, L. Evidence-based gene predictions in plant genomes. Genome Res. 19, 1912–1923 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2955">63</a></sup>. The evidence included 167 messenger RNAs and 25,310 ESTs of <i>Antirrhinum</i> from the NCBI nucleotide database (<a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov">https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov</a>), and SwissProt proteins for plants, which were cleaned up by removing redundant sequences with a minimum threshold of 80% for both identity and coverage, which left us with 340,312 sequences. Meanwhile, the mRNAs and ESTs of eudicot species were downloaded from NCBI and filtered to remove redundant sequences with a cut-off of 90% for both identity and coverage, resulting in 2,332,979 complementary DNAs and 152,396 ESTs, and RNA-seq data from six samples of <i>A. majus</i> were downloaded in this study and assembled into contigs using SOAPdenovo-trans v.1.03 (<a href="http://soap.genomics.org.cn/SOAPdenovo-Trans.html">http://soap.genomics.org.cn/SOAPdenovo-Trans.html</a>). The assembled contigs were used as same-species EST evidence. The genes with protein length &lt;100 amino acids and expression level in RNA-seq data &lt;1 RKPM were discarded. In the end, the predicted genes were obtained after selecting the longer ones between overlapping genes.</p><p>Gene functions were assigned according to the best match derived from the alignments to the integral database consisting of annotated proteins in <i>Arabidopsis</i> (<a href="https://www.arabidopsis.org/download_files/Proteins/TAIR10_protein_lists/TAIR10_pep_20101214">https://www.<i>arabidopsis</i>.org/download_files/Proteins/TAIR10_protein_lists/TAIR10_pep_20101214</a>) databases and SwissProt proteins using BLASTP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Altschul, S. F. &amp; Gish, W. Local alignment statistics. Methods Enzymo. 266, 460–480 (1996)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d14004e2997">55</a></sup>, with 30% minimum identity and coverage as threshold. We annotated motifs and domains using InterProScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Quevillon, E. et al. InterProScan: protein domains identifier. Nucleic Acids Res. 33, W116–W120 (2005)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3001">64</a></sup> by searching against publicly available databases, including ProDom<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Servant, F. et al. ProDom: Automated clustering of homologous domains. Brief. Bioinformatics 3, 246–251 (2002)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3005">65</a></sup> (<a href="http://prodom.prabi.fr/">http://prodom.prabi.fr/</a>), PRINTS<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Attwood, T. K. et al. The PRINTS Database: a fine-grained protein sequence annotation and analysis resource--its status in 2012. (Oxford, 2012)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3017">66</a></sup> (<a href="http://www.bioinf.manchester.ac.uk/dbbrowser/PRINTS/">www.bioinf.manchester.ac.uk/dbbrowser/PRINTS/</a>), Pfam<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Finn, R. D. et al. The Pfam protein families database: towards a more sustainable future. Nucleic Acids Res. 44, D279–D285 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3028">67</a></sup> (<a href="http://pfam.xfam.org/">http://pfam.xfam.org/</a>), SMART<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Letunic, I., Doerks, T. &amp; Bork, P. SMART: recent updates, new developments and status in 2015. Nucleic Acids Res. 43, D257–D260 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3039">68</a></sup> (<a href="http://smart.embl-heidelberg.de">http://smart.embl-heidelberg.de</a>/), PANTHER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Mi, H. et al. PANTHER version 11: expanded annotation data from Gene Ontology and Reactome pathways, and data analysis tool enhancements. Nucleic Acids Res. 45, D183–D189 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3051">69</a></sup> (<a href="http://www.pantherdb.org/">http://www.pantherdb.org/</a>), SUPERFAMILY<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Gough, J., Karplus, K., Hughey, R. &amp; Chothia, C. Assignment of homology to genome sequences using a library of hidden Markov models that represent all proteins of known structure. J. Mol. Biol. 313, 903–919 (2001)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3062">70</a></sup> (<a href="http://supfam.org/SUPERFAMILY/">http://supfam.org/SUPERFAMILY/</a>), PIR (<a href="http://pir.georgetown.edu/">http://pir.georgetown.edu/</a>) and PROSITE (<a href="http://prosite.expasy.org/">http://prosite.expasy.org/</a>). Both CPC program<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Kong, L. et al. CPC: assess the protein-coding potential of transcripts using sequence features and support vector machine. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, W345–W349 (2007)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3088">71</a></sup> and gene prediction evidence such as poor coding ability and protein length were used to filter the non-coding genes. All data for the evidence-based prediction were downloaded from corresponding databases on 5 January 2017, with the minimal length of 150 bp per 50 amino acids.</p><p>The <i>tRNA</i> genes were identified by tRNA scan-SE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Lowe, T. M. &amp; Eddy, S. R. tRNAscan-SE: a program for improved detection of transfer RNA genes in genomic sequence. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 955–964 (1997)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3098">72</a></sup> (<a href="https://wiki.gacrc.uga.edu/wiki/TRNAscan-SE">https://wiki.gacrc.uga.edu/wiki/TRNAscan-SE</a>) with eukaryote parameters. For rRNA identification, we aligned the <i>A. thaliana</i> rRNA sequences against the <i>A. majus</i> genome by using BLASTN<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Altschul, S. F. &amp; Gish, W. Local alignment statistics. Methods Enzymo. 266, 460–480 (1996)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3116">55</a></sup> with an <i>E</i> value of 1 × 10<sup>-5</sup>. The snRNA and miRNA predictions were made using INFERNAL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Nawrocki, E. P. &amp; Eddy, S. R. Infernal 1.1: 100-fold faster RNA homology searches. Bioinformatics 29, 2933–2935 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3125">73</a></sup> software (<a href="http://eddylab.org/infernal/">http://eddylab.org/infernal/</a>) and by searching against the Rfam<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Kalvari, I. et al. Rfam 13.0: shifting to a genome-centric resource for non-coding RNA families. Nucleic Acids Res. 46, D335–D342 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3136">74</a></sup> database (<a href="http://rfam.xfam.org/">http://rfam.xfam.org/</a>).</p><p>The classification of genes into families was carried out by BLASTP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Altschul, S. F. &amp; Gish, W. Local alignment statistics. Methods Enzymo. 266, 460–480 (1996)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3151">55</a></sup> all-against-all comparisons of predicted proteins using the duplicate_gene_classifier module integrated within MCScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Wang, Y. et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, e49 (2012)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3155">75</a></sup> (<a href="http://chibba.pgml.uga.edu/mcscan2/">http://chibba.pgml.uga.edu/mcscan2/</a>) with default parameters. The MCScan software classified the duplicate genes of one genome into whole genome /segmental (≥5 homologous gene pairs in collinear blocks), tandem (consecutive repeat), proximal (in nearby chromosomal region but adjacent within 10 genes) or dispersed (modes other than segmental, tandem and proximal) duplications. Remaining genes were defined as singletons. The iTAK<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Zheng, Y. et al. iTAK: A program for genome-wide prediction and classification of plant transcription factors, transcriptional regulators, and protein kinases. Mol. Plant 9, 1667–1670 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3166">76</a></sup> database (<a href="http://itak.feilab.net/cgi-bin/itak/index.cgi">http://itak.feilab.net/cgi-bin/itak/index.cgi</a>) was used to analyse transcription factor family expansion and to assign genes to specific families.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Genome repeat element identification</h3><p>Repetitive sequences and transposable elements in the genome were identified using a combination of de novo and homology-based approaches at both the DNA and protein levels. Briefly, we first constructed a de novo repeat library for snapdragon by using LTR_FINDER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Xu, Z. &amp; Wang, H. LTR_FINDER: an efficient tool for the prediction of full-length LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, W265–W268 (2007)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3186">77</a></sup> (<a href="http://tlife.fudan.edu.cn/ltr_finder/">http://tlife.fudan.edu.cn/ltr_finder/</a>) and passed this to Repeat Modeler<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Smit, A. F. A. &amp; Hubley, R. RepeatModeler Open-1.0, V.1.0.11 (Institute for Systems Biology, 2008–2015); http://www.repeatmasker.org" href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3197">78</a></sup> v.1.08 with default parameters. This library was aligned to the PGSB Repeat Element Database (<a href="http://pgsb.helmholtz-muenchen.de/plant/recat/">http://pgsb.helmholtz-muenchen.de/plant/recat/</a>) to generate the classification information for each repeat family. For identification of transposable elements at the DNA level, RepeatMasker was applied using both the repeat database we had built and Repbase<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Jurka, J. et al. Repbase Update, a database of eukaryotic repetitive elements. Cytogenet. Genome. Res. 110, 462–467 (2005)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3208">79</a></sup> (<a href="http://www.girinst.org/repbase">http://www.girinst.org/repbase</a>). Next, we executed RepeatProteinMask<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Smit, A. F. A. &amp; Hubley, R. RepeatModeler Open-1.0, V.1.0.11 (Institute for Systems Biology, 2008–2015); http://www.repeatmasker.org" href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3220">78</a></sup> (<a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/</a>) in a WU-BLASTX search against the transposable element protein database to further identify repeat-related proteins. The overlapping transposable elements belonging to the same repeat class were collated and combined according to the coordination in the genome. In addition, we annotated the tandem repeats by using the software Tandem Repeats Finder<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Benson, G. Tandem repeats finder: a program to analyze DNA sequences. Nucleic Acids Res. 27, 573–580 (1999)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3231">80</a></sup> (<a href="http://tandem.bu.edu/trf/trf.html">http://tandem.bu.edu/trf/trf.html</a>).</p><p>The full-length <i>Tam</i> sequences were retrieved from the NCBI nucleotide database and used to query the genome with BLASTN (v.4x10, -minIdentity=70). Hits with more than 20% query alignment coverage were retrieved with genomic coordinates. These sequences were then subjected to group analysis with blastclust (-S100-L0.99) integrated within NCBI BLAST (blast-2.2.25). Candidate recent active clusters were further examined by self-BLASTN of member sequences within these clusters and were considered supported where 100% query coverage and 100% identity (without mismatch or indels) were reported. For <i>Tam1</i>, <i>Tam2</i>, <i>Tam4</i> and <i>Tam11</i>, there was only one full-length <i>Tam</i> sequence detected. For <i>Tam3</i>, BLAST searches using each of five different full-length <i>Tam3</i> sequence accessions (AB012941, 3,698 bp; AB005454, 3577 bp; AB038403, 3488 bp; AB038404, 3601 bp; AB038404, 3,611 bp) produced similar results to the initial cloned <i>Tam3</i> (X55078, 3,629 bp) and confirmed that the <i>A. majus</i> genome sequenced in this study did not have a recent active cluster.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Gene family and synteny</h3><p>To identify gene family groups, we analysed protein-coding genes from nine plant species, <i>A. majus</i> (this study), <i>S. tuberosum</i> (<a href="ftp://ftp.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/genomes/Solanum_tuberosum/">ftp://ftp.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/genomes/Solanum_tuberosum/</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Xu, X. et al. Genome sequence and analysis of tuber crop potato. Nature 475, 189–195 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3297">81</a></sup>, <i>P. axillaris</i> (<a href="ftp://ftp.solgenomics.net/genomes/Petunia_axillaris/">ftp://ftp.solgenomics.net/genomes/Petunia_axillaris/</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Bombarely, A. et al. Insight into the evolution of the Solanaceae from the parental genomes of Petunia hybrida. Nat. Plants 2, 16074 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3312">82</a></sup>, <i>P. inflata</i> (<a href="ftp://ftp.solgenomics.net/genomes/Petunia_inflata/">ftp://ftp.solgenomics.net/genomes/Petunia_inflata/</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Bombarely, A. et al. Insight into the evolution of the Solanaceae from the parental genomes of Petunia hybrida. Nat. Plants 2, 16074 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3326">82</a></sup>, <i>S. lycopersicum</i> (<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/genome/annotation_euk/Solanum_lycopersicum/101/">http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/genome/annotation_euk/Solanum_lycopersicum/101/</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="The Tomato Genome Consortium. The tomato genome sequence provides insights into fleshy fruit evolution. Nature 485, 635–641 (2012)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3341">83</a></sup>, <i>A. thaliana</i> (<a href="https://www.arabidopsis.org/">https://www.arabidopsis.org/, TAIR10</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Arabidopsis Genome Initiative. Analysis of the genome sequence of the flowering plant Arabidopsis thaliana. Nature 408, 796–815 (2000)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3355">84</a></sup>, <i>C. papaya</i> (<a href="http://www.plantgdb.org/CpGDB/">http://www.plantgdb.org/CpGDB/, v1. 81</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 85" title="Ming, R. et al. The draft genome of the transgenic tropical fruit tree papaya (Carica papaya Linnaeus). Nature 452, 991–996 (2008)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3370">85</a></sup>, <i>P. mume</i> (<a href="https://www.rosaceae.org/">https://www.rosaceae.org/, v2.0.a1</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="Zhang, Q. et al. The genome of Prunus mume. Nat. Commun. 3, 1318 (2012)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3384">86</a></sup>, <i>V. vinifera</i> (<a href="http://www.genoscope.cns.fr/externe/Download/Projets/Projet_ML/data/12X/">http://www.genoscope.cns.fr/externe/Download/Projets/Projet_ML/data/12X/</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 87" title="Jaillon, O. et al. The grapevine genome sequence suggests ancestral hexaploidization in major angiosperm phyla. Nature 449, 463–467 (2007)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3399">87</a></sup>, <i>O</i>. <i>sativa</i> (<a href="http://rice.plantbiology.msu.edu/">http://rice.plantbiology.msu.edu/</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 88" title="Kawahara, Y. et al. Improvement of the Oryza sativa Nipponbare reference genome using next generation sequence and optical map data. Rice 6, 4 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR88" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3416">88</a></sup> and <i>A. trichopod</i> (<a href="http://www.amborella.org/">http://www.amborella.org/</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 89" title="Rice, D. W. et al. Horizontal transfer of entire genomes via mitochondrial fusion in the angiosperm. Amborella. Science. 342, 1468–1473 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR89" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3431">89</a></sup>. We performed an all-against-all comparison using BLASTP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Majoros, W. H., Pertea, M. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics 20, 2878–2879 (2004)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3435">57</a></sup> with an <i>E</i> value cut-off of 1 × 10<sup>-5</sup>, and the OrthoMCL method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 90" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C. J. Jr. &amp; Roos, D. S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178–2189 (2003)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR90" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3445">90</a></sup> was used to cluster the BLASTP results into paralogous and orthologous clusters.</p><p>In total, 2,115 single-copy gene families were used to reconstruct the phylogenetic tree. First, the proteins of single-copy gene families were aligned by MUSCLE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 91" title="Edgar, R. C. MUSCLE: a multiple sequence alignment method with reduced time and space complexity. BMC Bioinformatics 5, 113 (2004)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR91" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3452">91</a></sup>. Following alignment, the protein was reverse-transcribed into the coding sequence and four-fold degenerate sites were extracted from each alignment and concatenated to create one super gene for each species. We used jModelTest to select the best model (<a href="http://darwin.uvigo.es">http://darwin.uvigo.es</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 92" title="Posada, D. jModelTest: phylogenetic model averaging. Mol. Biol. Evol. 25, 1253–1256 (2008)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR92" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3463">92</a></sup>. PhyML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 93" title="Guindon, S., Lethiec, F., Duroux, P. &amp; Gascuel, O. PHYML Online—a web server for fast maximum likelihood‐based phylogenetic inference. Nucleic Acids Res. 33, W557–W559 (2005)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR93" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3467">93</a></sup> was used to construct the phylogenetic tree using the JTT+I+GAMMA model and 1,000 bootstrap replicates. We used a similar method to PGDD (<a href="http://chibba.agtec.uga.edu/duplication/">http://chibba.agtec.uga.edu/duplication/</a>) to identify WGD events within the <i>A. majus</i> genome. Proteins were aligned to each other with BLASTP and a filter threshold of 1 × 10<sup>-5</sup> was used to identify homologous proteins. MCScanX<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Wang, Y. et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, e49 (2012)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3484">75</a></sup> with default parameters (<a href="http://chibba.pgml.uga.edu/mcscan2/">http://chibba.pgml.uga.edu/mcscan2/</a>) was used to find collinear blocks, each containing at least five collinear gene pairs. The Ks value was calculated with the PAML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 94" title="Yang, Z. et al. PAML: a program package for phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Comput. Appl. Biosci. 13, 555–556 (1997)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR94" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3495">94</a></sup> yn00 NG model (<a href="http://abacus.gene.ucl.ac.uk/software/paml.html">http://abacus.gene.ucl.ac.uk/software/paml.html</a>). Intragenome dot plot comparison of <i>A. majus</i> was carried out using the SynMap tool from the online CoGe portal<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 95" title="Nelson, A. D. L., Haug-Baltzell, A. K., Davey, S., Gregory, B. D. &amp; Lyons, E. EPIC-CoGe: managing and analyzing genomic data. Bioinformatics 34, 2651–2653 (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR95" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3510">95</a></sup> (<a href="http://genomevolution.org/CoGe/">http://genomevolution.org/CoGe/</a>). GEvo microsyntenic analysis of each collinear block was performed using SynMap and SynFind also in the CoGe portal. The divergence times of <i>C. papaya</i><b>–</b><i>A. thaliana</i> (~55.1–90.6 Ma) and dicot–monocot (~123.9–228.5 Ma) were used for calibration.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Transcriptome analysis</h3><p>Total RNA was isolated from the leaf, pistil, pollen, root, stamen and stem. For tissues with large biomass (leaf, root and stem), each tissue mixture was obtained from three plants. For the rest of the tissues (pistil, pollen and stamen), each tissue mixture was sampled from at least 10 plants. All plants used in RNA-seq were growth at the environment as that used for genome sequencing and were confirmed with consistent growth. RNA sequencing libraries (300–500 bp fragments) were constructed using the mRNA-Seq Prep Kit (Illumina). Then, we sequenced all libraries using Illumina HiSeq 2000 (2 × 100 bp). FastQC<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 96" title="Andrews, S. FastQC: a quality control tool for high throughput sequence data. v.0.11.8 (Brabham Bioinformatics, Brabham Institute, 2010); &#xA;                    http://www.bioinformatics.babraham.ac.uk/projects/fastqc&#xA;                    &#xA;                  &#xA;                        " href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR96" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3536">96</a></sup> qualified reads ware mapped to the genome guided by the final gene model using hisat2 (<a href="http://www.bioinformatics.babraham.ac.uk/projects/fastqc">http://www.bioinformatics.babraham.ac.uk/projects/fastqc</a>) and the expression level for each gene was calculated by Stringtie<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 97" title="Pertea, M., Kim, D., Pertea, G. M., Leek, J. T. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. Transcript-level expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with HISAT, StringTie and Ballgown. Nat. Protoc. 11, 1650–1667 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR97" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3547">97</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Construction of BAC library</h3><p>High-molecular-weight DNA of over 2 Mb from <i>Antirrhinum</i> (<i>A. majus</i> JI7 line) was extracted from leaf nuclei according to Liu and Whitter<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 98" title="Liu, Y. &amp; Whitter, R. Rapid preparation of megabase plant DNA from nuclei in agarose plugs and microbeads. Nucleic Acids Res. 22, 2168–2169 (1994)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR98" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3565">98</a></sup> and partially digested with <i>Hin</i>dIII. BAC vector preparation, ligation and transformation of <i>TranformMaxTM EP1300TM Escherichia coli</i> (EPICENTRE Biotechnologies) by electroporation followed the described method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 99" title="Shizuya, H. et al. Cloning and stable maintenance of 300-kilobase-pair fragments of human DNA in Escherichia coli using an F-factor-based vector. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 89, 8794–8797 (1992)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR99" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3576">99</a></sup>. BAC DNA was digested with <i>Hin</i>dIII and sized-fractioned with a field inversion agarose gel electrophoresis to estimate the insert length. A total of 114,816 clones were selected and stored in 384-well plates.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">FISH</h3><p>Immature 1.5–3.0 mm <i>Antirrhinum</i> flower buds were harvested and fixed in Carnoy’s solution (ethanol:glacial acetic acid, 3:1) and stored at –20 °C. BAC clones were isolated and labelled with digoxigenin-16-dUTP or biotin-11-dUTP by nick translation. FISH was performed on the pachytene chromosomes as described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 98" title="Liu, Y. &amp; Whitter, R. Rapid preparation of megabase plant DNA from nuclei in agarose plugs and microbeads. Nucleic Acids Res. 22, 2168–2169 (1994)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR98" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3594">98</a></sup>. Chromosomes were counterstained with 4’6-diamindino-phenylindole (DAPI) in an antifade solution. Chromosomes and FISH signal images were captured with an Olympus BX53 fluorescence microscope conjunct with a micro charge-coupled device camera. Three experiments were performed<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 100" title="Jiang, J., Gill, B. S., Wang, G. L., Ronald, P. C. &amp; Ward, D. C. Metaphase and interphase fluorescence in situ hybridization mapping of the rice genome with bacterial artificial chromosomes. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 92, 4487–4491 (1995)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR100" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3598">100</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Evolutionary analysis of TCP family genes</h3><p>Syntenic block identification and Ks analyses were carried out using MCscanX<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Wang, Y. et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, e49 (2012)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3610">75</a></sup> and the PAML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 94" title="Yang, Z. et al. PAML: a program package for phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Comput. Appl. Biosci. 13, 555–556 (1997)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR94" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3614">94</a></sup> yn00 NG model, respectively. MEGA7<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 101" title="Kumar, S., Stecher, G. &amp; Tamura, K. MEGA7: Molecular Evolutionary Genetics Analysis Version 7.0 for Bigger Datasets. Mol. Biol. Evol. 33, 1870–1874 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR101" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3618">101</a></sup> was used for the multiple alignment and phylogentic tree construction. Expression pattern was carried out with MeV. TF family annotation was carried out using the website of plantTFDB (<a href="http://planttfdb.cbi.pku.edu.cn/prediction.php">http://planttfdb.cbi.pku.edu.cn/prediction.php</a>).</p><p>The annotations and sequences of <i>Aquilegia coerulea</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 102" title="Filiault, D. et al. The Aquilegia genome: adaptive radiation and an extraordinarily polymorphic chromosome with a unique history. Preprint at bioRxiv &#xA;                    https://doi.org/10.1101/264101&#xA;                    &#xA;                   (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR102" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3634">102</a></sup> were downloaded from the website <a href="https://img.jgi.doe.gov/">https://img.jgi.dofor exampleov/</a>. <i>Phalaenopsis equestris</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 103" title="Cai, J. et al. The genome sequence of the orchid Phalaenopsis equestris. Nat. Genet. 47, 65–72 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR103" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3647">103</a></sup> was downloaded from <a href="http://orchidbase.itps.ncku.edu.tw/">http://orchidbase.itps.ncku.edu.tw/</a>.</p><p><i>Petunia axillaris</i> and <i>Petunia inflata</i> were downloaded from <a href="https://solgenomics.net/organism/Petunia_axillaris/genome">https://solgenomics.net/organism/Petunia_axillaris/genome</a> and <a href="https://solgenomics.net/organism/Petunia_inflata/genome">https://solgenomics.net/organism/Petunia_inflata/genome</a>, respectively.</p><p>The functional known protein members in TCP families were downloaded from the original experimental papers and used as marker proteins for TCP subfamily identification. Two putative TCP family genes (<i>Am03g34120</i> with partial TCP domains and <i>Am01g42140</i> with two tandem TCP domains) were excluded from phylogenetic analyses. Syntenic block and Ks analysis detected three gene pairs derived from WGD. <i>Am08g22680</i>/<i>Am06g32830</i> (Ks = 0.99) and <i>Am08g20570</i>/<i>Am06g35450</i> (Ks = 0.76) were located in a large syntenic block with 79 homologous gene pairs (median Ks = 0.85), while <i>Am08g18340</i>/<i>Am06g39840</i> (Ks = 0.58) were located in a block with 11 homologous gene pairs (median Ks = 1.01).</p><p>Known MYB family TFs involved in zygomorphic flower control, <i>DIV</i> (Q8S9H7), <i>DIVL</i>(AAL78742), <i>RAD</i>(Q58FS3), <i>DRIF-1</i>(AGL11918) and <i>DRIF-2</i> (AGL11919), were BlastP searched against the proteome. The protein sequences for the top two best hits were retrieved and confirmed by InterPro analysis. Retained duplicated copies derived from the WGD event were confirmed by both syntenic block and Ks analysis. Expression and function analysis identified <i>Lotus japonicus</i> <i>CYC</i> genes <i>LjCYC1</i> (DQ202475), <i>LjCYC2</i> (DQ202476), <i>LjCYC3</i> (DQ202477) and <i>LjCYC5</i> (DQ202478) that were used to BlastP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Majoros, W. H., Pertea, M. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics 20, 2878–2879 (2004)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3747">57</a></sup> search the <i>L japonicas</i> proteome. All three <i>CYC</i> genes could be detected with ≥98% amino acid identity except for <i>LjCYC2</i>, which was not detected with relaxed alignment criteria nor by Tblastn search <i>of</i> the <i>L. japonicas</i> genome (downloaded from <a href="http://chibba.agtec.uga.edu/duplication">http://chibba.agtec.uga.edu/duplication v.2.5</a>), strongly indicating that the <i>LjCYC2</i> gene was absent from the current <i>L. japonicas</i> assembly.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Genome-wide search for <i>S</i>-gene candidates in <i>Antirrhinum</i> and related plant species</h3><p>Except for the genome data set of <i>Antirrhinum</i>, the recently published or revised versions of the other 14 genome data sets were downloaded from their public websites (Supplementary Data Set <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#MOESM3">14</a>). Published SLF protein sequences of <i>Antirrhinum</i> were separately used to establish the group-specific SLF profiles of Plantaginaceae.</p><p>Alignments were verified manually, and a consensus sequence was created for each of the motifs of interest with the help of the Weblogo software package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 104" title="Crooks, G. E., Hon, G., Chandonia, J. M. &amp; Brenner, S. E. WebLogo: A sequence logo generator. Genome Res. 14, 1188–1190 (2004)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR104" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3808">104</a></sup>. This alignment was used to generate an HMM model using the program hmmbuild from the HMMER program suite40. Using hmmsearch, the HMM model was applied in a search against the most recent protein annotations from each plant species. To confirm the presence of both F-box and Kelch/FBA1/FBA3 domains in the obtained sequences (<i>E</i> &lt; 10<sup>–30</sup>), we further compared the results from hmmsearch and the Pfam databases with the hmmpfam package. Our domains of interest were annotated in Pfam as PF00646 (F-box), PF04300 (FBA1), PF08268 (FBA3) and PF01344 (Kelch domain 1).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Reporting Summary</h3><p>Further information on research design is available in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#MOESM2">Nature Research Reporting Summary</a> linked to this article.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>Genome assembly data have been deposited at NCBI BioProject ID under accession codes <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJNA227267">PRJNA227267</a>. The raw sequence data reported in this paper have been deposited in the Genome Sequence Archive<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 105" title="Wang, Y. et al. GSA: Genome Sequence Archive. Genomics Proteomics Bioinformatics 15, 14–18 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR105" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3888">105</a></sup> in the BIG Data Center<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 106" title="BIG Data Center Members. The BIG Data Center: from deposition to integration to translation. Nucleic Acids Res. 45, D18–D24 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0349-9#ref-CR106" id="ref-link-section-d14004e3892">106</a></sup>, Beijing Institute of Genomics (BIG), Chinese Academy of Sciences, under accession numbers <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJCA000223">PRJCA000223</a> and <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJCA001050">PRJCA001050</a> that are publicly accessible at <a href="http://bigd.big.ac.cn/gsa">http://bigd.big.ac.cn/gsa</a>. We built the <i>Antirrhinum</i> genome website at <a href="http://bioinfo.sibs.ac.cn/Am">http://bioinfo.sibs.ac.cn/Am</a>, providing a portal to genome browser, Blast, data download and gene expression functions. All data that support the findings of this study are also available from the corresponding authors upon request.</p>

              <p class="c-article-further-reading__journal-title" id="journal-name-2">
